The overall design of the hotel is very exquisite, Chinese and Jiangnan style. The persimmons that can be seen everywhere in the hotel also add a sense of warmth in autumn and winter. I like the scene of abundant and reunited persimmons, which matches the festive atmosphere at the end of the year.
It happened to be the end of autumn when we went there, and there were a lot of dried persimmons drying in front of the hotel, and I didn't know if I could buy them. After entering the hotel, I was simply surrounded by persimmons. There is a whole wall of persimmons at the front desk, and there seem to be more than 100 of them, representing the hotel's more than 100 guest rooms. There is a persimmon ornament at the door of each guest room, and the name of the guest room also uses the homophony of "persimmon" to find a four-character auspicious word (I feel that the elders must like it very much! There are also persimmon pillows and persimmon ornaments in the guest room... Lujing Xixi is like a persimmon ******
The guest rooms in the hotel are quite large, and the design is quite special. The partitions are well done, and it really feels like home. The aunt in the guest room will give you a bowl of hot red bean soup when you turn down at night. Hotel robots deliver meals, and you can eat a lot of local delicacies (although Hangzhou is a food desert with residents).
Walking to the infinity pool on the top floor, it has a different kind of tranquility this season; when the wind blows, I hide in the study room on the second floor. The space is elegant but unusually warm. The shock of reading just now is gently and soothingly resolved, and I get up to go to the restaurant. After eating a bowl of garlic bean noodles that are as good as Xin Rong Ji's, I was thinking about my next destination, or Taizhou.
In summary, if you are taking your elders and children to travel to Hangzhou, it is still worth recommending. The environment is good enough, the facilities are complete, and you can also go to Xixi Wetland for a tour~
